  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_386b0d2b-dec9-4a77-95ec-435edd6bb1cd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div id="review_2449543099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449543099" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449543099?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781504028059" href="/book/show/27601308-six-days-of-the-condor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=spies">spies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449543099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3199966401232173600"><b>”This is Condor, Section 9, Department 17. <br/><br/>‘We’ve been hit.’”</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Redford20Condor203_zps2o3buoae.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532093812i/26002517.jpg' alt=' photo Redford20Condor203_zps2o3buoae.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Choose your own Condor. He can look like this.</b> <br/><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Condor20Max20Irons_zpsgalc6crh.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532093812i/26002518.jpg' alt=' photo Condor20Max20Irons_zpsgalc6crh.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Or like this.</b><br/><br/>Most days, Ronald Malcolm’s biggest worries were from which coffee pot on which floor he was going to get his dose of caffeine, what type of sandwich he was going to have at lunch, and not dawdling too long in the morning so he was at his work desk on time to admire the beautiful siren walking by his building every day. <br/><br/><b>Simple life for a normal guy.</b> <br/><br/>His job was not nor</span>
  <span id="freeText3199966401232173600" style="display:none"><b>”This is Condor, Section 9, Department 17. <br><br>‘We’ve been hit.’”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Redford20Condor203_zps2o3buoae.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532093812i/26002517.jpg" alt=" photo Redford20Condor203_zps2o3buoae.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Choose your own Condor. He can look like this.</b> <br><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Condor20Max20Irons_zpsgalc6crh.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532093812i/26002518.jpg" alt=" photo Condor20Max20Irons_zpsgalc6crh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Or like this.</b><br><br>Most days, Ronald Malcolm’s biggest worries were from which coffee pot on which floor he was going to get his dose of caffeine, what type of sandwich he was going to have at lunch, and not dawdling too long in the morning so he was at his work desk on time to admire the beautiful siren walking by his building every day. <br><br><b>Simple life for a normal guy.</b> <br><br>His job was not normal. It would be boring for a lot of people, but for someone like me, it would be a dream job. He worked in this nondescript building that was a front for a CIA operation. Not field work, or running secret agents, or working to take down a super villain while he was still a hoodlum. No, Ronald’s job was reading spy thrillers and mysteries. <br><br><b>He was paid to read.</b> <br><br>His job was to read these books and take notes of anything that happens that might be of use to the CIA at some point and time. <br><br>If the CIA is reading this review, I just want to say I am an expert reader. I take copious notes of what I read. I have an impressive resume of thrillers I’ve already read so I would be attuned to discovering things I’ve never read before in a book. <br><br><b>PM me, Big Brother.</b> <br><br>The plot swung into action when a hit squad came in and killed everyone in the building. Except for one.<br><br>Ronald was out grabbing a sandwich, crumbs were still clinging to the edges of his mouth as he stared at the bodies of his colleagues lying in pools of blood . Great, right? What a stroke of dumb luck, but it proved to be harder than one would expect for Ronald/Condor to come in for a debriefing. <b>He became The Spy Thriller Reader Who Tried to Come in From the Cold.</b><br><br>Things were more dire than just people trying to kill him. He was out in the cold...bookless. It gave me the shivers. <br><br>I’ve watched the 1975 Robert Redford movie with the lovely Faye Dunaway numerous times, and the movie is terrific. They cut the expanse of time that the story unfolds from six days down to three. I’m currently enjoying the new TV series called <i>Condor</i> on the Audience channel. The series stars Max Irons, the son of the great Jeremy Irons, and it has become must see TV in my house. I always enjoy seeing the interpretation of the same story by different writers and directors. <i>Six Days of the Condor</i> was sold to Hollywood even before the book was published. <br><br>There is a fascinating preface to the Open Road edition written by James Grady that discusses the process of how he got the idea for the book and, most interesting of all, how the Redford movie created quite the flurry of worry in KGB headquarters. <br><br><b>”An exposé published in 2008 by Pete Early--a story sanctioned by America’s FBI and CIA--revealed that the movie stunned the KGB generals and convinced them that they had fallen behind their CIA foes in what had to be a critical espionage endeavor: the work they saw Redford/Condor doing in the movie.”</b><br><br>The KGB designed almost a carbon copy of the building and formed a research department to try and catch up with this mythical (tell me it isn’t so) department of the CIA. Another example of life being too bizarre for fiction. The movie did deviate from the book, but the true essence of the story was retained by the director, Sydney Pollack. The book moved along at a quick pace with some nail biting scenes that were impressions coming from a 24 year old, first time novelist. I am now officially a Condor expert. This is another nice addition to my resume in case the CIA ever wants a willing recruit to open Department 17 for real. <br><br>I’m always going to be the guy who goes for sandwiches. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3199966401232173600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2539783048" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2539783048" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2539783048?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36687064-six-days-of-the-condor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539783048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12347986080534589446">My introduction to the fiction of James Grady is his 1974 debut novel <i>Six Days of the Condor</i>. Even more so than Peter Benchley, the author is one whose credentials are easily established by mentioning the movie version of his book: <i>Three Days of the Condor</i>, released the same year as <i>Jaws</i>. Like <i>Jaws</i>, <i>Three Days of the Condor</i> made liberal changes to its source material. Like <i>Jaws</i>, that source material is so far away from the movie in terms of quality that it isn't in the same ballpark, parking lot</span>
  <span id="freeText12347986080534589446" style="display:none">My introduction to the fiction of James Grady is his 1974 debut novel <i>Six Days of the Condor</i>. Even more so than Peter Benchley, the author is one whose credentials are easily established by mentioning the movie version of his book: <i>Three Days of the Condor</i>, released the same year as <i>Jaws</i>. Like <i>Jaws</i>, <i>Three Days of the Condor</i> made liberal changes to its source material. Like <i>Jaws</i>, that source material is so far away from the movie in terms of quality that it isn't in the same ballpark, parking lot, or zip code as the film, a ridiculous star vehicle that was nonetheless memorably well-produced. This book is not.<br><br>The action takes place in Washington D.C., four blocks from the Library of Congress, where the most edible chicken nugget of the book introduces the "American Literary Historical Society," a front for Department 17 of the CIA. The Society keeps track of all espionage related acts in literature, monitoring potential security leaks and looking for new ideas. Far from books, Ronald Malcolm is an analyst obsessed with an "incredibly beautiful" blonde who mounts the steps of the Library of Congress each morning. He yawns his way through a meeting with their new accountant, who's puzzled by a shipment in which seven crates appear on a billing order but only five were received.<br><br>Following a memo the accountant sends to Langley, two plainclothes men visit him at his apartment. The next afternoon, Malcolm slips out a coalbin exit in the basement to pick up lunch. While he's out, three assassins gain access to the office and gun down Malcolm's four male and two female co-workers. Discovering the grisly scene, Malcolm phones Langely from a pay phone using his code name "Condor" to let the agency know his substation has been hit. The head of Department 17 goes into the field to bring Condor in but attempts to kill him. Malcolm abducts a young paralegal named Wendy Ross and enlists her aid to outwit his assassins.<br><br><i>"I don't believe you." The girl sat on the couch, her eyes glued to Malcolm. She was not as frightened as she had been, but her heart felt as if it was breaking ribs.<br><br>Malcolm sighed. He had been sitting across from the girl for an hour. From what he found in her purse, he knew she was Wendy Ross, twenty-seven years old, had lived and driven in Carbondale, Illinois, distributed 135 pounds on her five-foot-ten frame (he was sure that was an overestimated lie), regularly gave Type O Positive blood to the Red Cross, was a card-carrying user of the Alexandria Public Library and a member of the University of Southern Illinois Alumni Association, and was certified to receive and deliver summonses for her employers, Bechtel, Barber, Sievers, Holloran, and Muclkeston. From what he read on her face, he knew she was frightened and telling the truth when she said she didn't believe him. Malcolm didn't blame her, as he really didn't believe his story either, and he knew it was true.<br><br>"Look," he said, "If what I said wasn't true, why would I try to convince you it was?"<br><br>"I don't know."<br><br>"Oh, Jesus!" Malcolm paced the room. He could tie her up and still use her place, but that was risky. Besides, she could be invaluable. He had an inspiration in the middle of a sneeze.</i><br><br>Oh, Jesus. <i>Six Days of the Condor</i> is full of flat and shabby prose. Characters are introduced in much the way a ten-year-old might: a distinguished looking man, a second man, etc. Malcolm is so devoid of personality that a stereotype would've been an improvement. He is not a book nerd, nor is he a soldier type, nor is he a rake. Any of these personalities might explain his ability to evade professional killers, but instead, Malcolm lives by virtue of his blind luck and the fallacies of his pursuers. Wendy is a nubile piece of candy as useless in the field as Malcolm and so dumb enough that's she'd rather fuck this bar of Spam than escape him.<br><br>Grady's approach reminded me of Tom Clancy, who'd debut ten years later with guy-oriented espionage thrillers that jumped between government agencies, with detail only someone obsessed enough by the CIA to read technical manuals could divine. Grady doesn't demonstrate the hard-on for hardware that Clancy would and as a result, <i>Six Days of the Condor</i> is 90,000 words lighter than <i>The Hunt For Red October</i>. The disappointment of Grady is the monumental disinterest for books he demonstrates given his literary set-up. Other than one mention of Poe, Malcolm's skills as a librarian go completely unused.<br><br>The 2011 edition published by MysteriousPress.com/ Open Road contains a preface by Grady that constitutes a whopping 15% of the book. The author recounts how influential he was on the geopolitical scene and what it was like working with director Sydney Pollack on the movie. Ugh. Released in 1975, <i>Three Days of the Condor</i> moved the action to New York City. Robert Redford played CIA analyst Joe Turner and Faye Dunaway, playing a photographer named Kathy Hale, his captive. Rather than <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[heroin smuggling <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, a rogue operation to seize Middle Eastern oil fields is the plot. The <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lcgDAwus9WA" rel="nofollow noopener">assault on Redford's office</a> is a highlight of the film, along with a terrific jazz-infused score by Dave Grusin.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554851577i/27340464._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Length: 57,411 words</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12347986080534589446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_265991249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265991249" />
    <a title="Checkman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117003-checkman"><img alt="Checkman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591798821p2/5117003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265991249?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Checkman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Checkman" href="/user/show/5117003-checkman">Checkman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 044007570X" href="/book/show/648916.Six_Days_of_the_Condor">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of conspiracies</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=beach-read">beach-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=seventies-classics">seventies-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265991249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17133157257161453077">One of the all time classic paranoid thrillers of the 1970's and a sentimental favorite of mine. James Grady's first novel, written and published when he was in in his mid-twenties. It's very much a product of the time when he wrote it. Watergate paranoia, Vietnam, disillusionment with the U.S. government, the anti-authority attitude of the Baby Boomers and more all play a part in the plot.<br/><br/>To younger readers the plot will seem unoriginal. A low level intelligence analyst stumbles across a conspi</span>
  <span id="freeText17133157257161453077" style="display:none">One of the all time classic paranoid thrillers of the 1970's and a sentimental favorite of mine. James Grady's first novel, written and published when he was in in his mid-twenties. It's very much a product of the time when he wrote it. Watergate paranoia, Vietnam, disillusionment with the U.S. government, the anti-authority attitude of the Baby Boomers and more all play a part in the plot.<br /><br />To younger readers the plot will seem unoriginal. A low level intelligence analyst stumbles across a conspiracy hidden within the government's intelligence community (without really understanding what it is he's discovered), becomes a marked man and has to go on the run.<br /><br />While on the run he has to try to figure out who and what has marked him for death. Not very original. Until one takes into account that this story was one of the first.....of it's kind. When the reader realizes this fact the novel can be enjoyed for what it is. <br /><br />A short and fast moving story that still has the ability to pull the reader in. Of course there are aspects of it that are dated (mostly in terms of information technology), but that's inevitable. Like William Goldman's classic novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21796.Marathon_Man" title="Marathon Man by William Goldman" rel="nofollow noopener">Marathon Man</a> I like the fact that the characters have to rely on their skills and luck rather than a plethora of high-tech devices to help them out. <br /><br />Mr. Grady's focus is on suspense and moving the plot along. His writing is tight and economical. All in all it's an impressive first novel. Mr. Grady has written many other novels in the decades that have followed and his writing has improved. His characters have gotten deeper, his plots more intricate, the sex less detailed and the moral tones a bit more grey. In other words Mr. Grady has gotten older (as do we all) and his books reflect this. But <i> Six Days of the Condor </i> is an entertaining read and an easy way to pass a few hours. I recommend it if you know you're going to have several hours on your hands. Waiting in an airport, spending time in a hospital waiting room etc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17133157257161453077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1587913126" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1587913126" />
    <a title="Fred Shaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44212467-fred-shaw"><img alt="Fred Shaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545362118p2/44212467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_127468183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127468183" />
    <a title="Eric_W" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w"><img alt="Eric_W" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550592937p2/1711431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127468183?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric_W" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric_W" href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w">Eric_W</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=spies">spies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127468183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12944295531520188">In an introduction to the audiobook, Grady provides some background on how he, and the intelligence community, were influenced by this book. He happened to be wandering down a street when he imagined that behind one of the doors was a secret CIA research bureau. And then he wondered what would have happened if one of the workers left and returned to find all his colleagues dead. Grady learned in 2008 from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1911762.Comrade_J' title='Comrade J by Pete Earley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Comrade J</a> by Pete Early, that the Russians assumed from watching the Redford movie that thi</span>
  <span id="freeText12944295531520188" style="display:none">In an introduction to the audiobook, Grady provides some background on how he, and the intelligence community, were influenced by this book. He happened to be wandering down a street when he imagined that behind one of the doors was a secret CIA research bureau. And then he wondered what would have happened if one of the workers left and returned to find all his colleagues dead. Grady learned in 2008 from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1911762.Comrade_J" title="Comrade J by Pete Earley" rel="nofollow noopener">Comrade J</a> by Pete Early, that the Russians assumed from watching the Redford movie that this was the way the CIA conducted business, and they formed a 2,000 man secret bureau devoted to doing the kind of research now so common in movies and shows such as Rubicon. “What if, became what was.”<br /><br />The prosaic reason why the movie was shot in New York instead of Washington ,where the book takes place, was simply because Robert Redford was due to shoot All the President’s Men which had to take place in Washington and he didn’t want to leave his family in New York for the duration of two movies.<br /><br />This was Grady’s first book and smashed in between interesting scenes of intrigue are rather awkward moments of silliness. The love scene between Wendy and Malcolm (he has just kidnapped her. then persuaded her that he’s not a bad guy, taken a shower and had dinner together) was in such purple prose as to be almost comical and the next morning she “mounts” him again (shades of Fanny Hill, I’m surprised it wasn’t his “member”) and then has to call a doctor friend for a house call because of Malcom’s vicious“strep throat.” <br /><br />Still as my GR friend Nancy notes, this is a real page-turner (or, at least, unable-to-shut-off-the-the-iPod-when-parking-in-the-garage.) It’s fun. I would make it 3 stars for the writing, five for the idea and plot, so we’ll round it off to 4 (in reality, probably 3.14159265, heh heh.)<br /><br />Nancy has a nice plot summary in her review. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39280319">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12944295531520188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_319982865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319982865" />
    <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo"><img alt="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448623481p2/3615945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319982865?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo">Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842431931" href="/book/show/2983612-six-days-of-the-condor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=spring-2012">spring-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=permanent-library">permanent-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=suspense-intrigue">suspense-intrigue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=good-fiction">good-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319982865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7175386842886926282"><b>5 Stars</b><br/> <br/><u>SUMMARY</u><br/><br/>In the quiet Washington D.C. neighborhood near the Capitol is a pristine townhouse. Its plaque reads American Literary Historical Society. The headquarters ostensibly is for literary analysis, advance and achievement, but no one gets passed the front desk. Unless of course proper clearance is shown and verified. The Society is actually a Company Department Office. The research analysts read mystery and thriller novels and pass any scenarios that are too close to the mark of past a</span>
  <span id="freeText7175386842886926282" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br /> <br /><u>SUMMARY</u><br /><br />In the quiet Washington D.C. neighborhood near the Capitol is a pristine townhouse. Its plaque reads American Literary Historical Society. The headquarters ostensibly is for literary analysis, advance and achievement, but no one gets passed the front desk. Unless of course proper clearance is shown and verified. The Society is actually a Company Department Office. The research analysts read mystery and thriller novels and pass any scenarios that are too close to the mark of past and or present operations. An analyst finds discrepancies in book deliveries and has questioned all of the researchers. All is not right in RD. <br /> <br />Upon his arrival with his colleagues lunches Malcolm, codenamed Condor, discovers his friends butchered in a blood-spattered office. He realizes that an oversight by the assassins has saved his life. He contacts CIA headquarters through the Panic line for assistance and direction. But the attempted rendezvous goes horribly wrong. Malcolm quickly learns that he can’t trust anyone and disappears into the streets of the Capitol, hoping to evade the killers long enough to unravel the conspiracy. But will that be enough to save his life? <br /><br /> <br /><u>MY THOUGHTS</u><br /> <br />1.) It’s hard to believe that 38 years have past since <i>Condor</i> was 1st published and then rushed into film. I can’t separate Redford from Malcolm, nor do I want to. Another amazing fact is James Grady was only 24 when he wrote this sleek taut novel. His writing is succinct building the suspense by tightly threaded event sequences that quickly spin out of control. We are treated to 3 distinct POVs: Malcolm’s, the agents who want to save him, and those shadowy ones who don’t.<br /> <br />2.) Grady departs from the usual spy thrillers of that time. Malcolm is not a super-hero with fancy gadgets. His only weapons are his analytical intellect and the will to survive. When Grady’s characters get hurt, they hurt. No miraculous healing powers in his world.<br /><br />3.) Written before Watergate, the shadow government and it’s insistence that loose ends are swiftly and permanently cut worked in 1974 as they do today. Malcolm’s CIA department ignited readers’ imaginations and those of the KGB. In his Author’s Notes, Grady says he was surprised that the Soviets actually thought the<i>Condor’s</i> RD section existed and quickly formed their own equivalent to its fictional counterpart. Does that RD section now exist in the CIA? I wouldn’t put it past them. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7175386842886926282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1449183453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1449183453?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan Olesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan Olesen" href="/user/show/7050149-susan-olesen">Susan Olesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449183453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18264180559861578971">I almost NEVER quit on a book, but I quit this one after suffering 100 pages. It was so famous, I wanted to read it. But it was just bloody awful. Besides the unbelievable fact that the lead character kidnaps a woman, forces her at gunpoint to take him to her house, and then she just decides to climb into his bed and screw him that night? Really? I would have been out the door. It was so poorly written by today's standards that the main action - the very moment Malcolm finds out he might be bein</span>
  <span id="freeText18264180559861578971" style="display:none">I almost NEVER quit on a book, but I quit this one after suffering 100 pages. It was so famous, I wanted to read it. But it was just bloody awful. Besides the unbelievable fact that the lead character kidnaps a woman, forces her at gunpoint to take him to her house, and then she just decides to climb into his bed and screw him that night? Really? I would have been out the door. It was so poorly written by today's standards that the main action - the very moment Malcolm finds out he might be being double-crossed and his rescuer shoots at him - is all told in dull 3rd person description, all tell and no show. There is nothing to grab you and suck you into this story at all. <br /><br />I'm a library worker. I'm reading books all the time. I suffered through a number of ho-hum books, but made it to the end. I just couldn't bear to suffer with this one any longer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18264180559861578971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

Although the plot of the book differs from the film, the basic elements remain the same. The reason for the hit on "Condor's" department differs from that of the film version. Also, the book has a more definite ending than the film. A good read, but I just like the movie better.</span>

<div id="review_39280319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39280319" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39280319?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=spy-fiction">spy-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39280319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3780394882583141152">The national headquarters of the American Literary Historical Society is in Washington, DC, its purpose ostensibly for literary analysis, advance and achievement. No one goes there and takes tours -- they can't get past the main desk without proper clearance. In reality, it's a CIA office where people read and analyze mystery and spy novels (what a dream job!) to seek out correlations between fiction and fact. <br/><br/>One of the employees there, Ronald Malcolm, advises another employee (Heidegger) to ig</span>
  <span id="freeText3780394882583141152" style="display:none">The national headquarters of the American Literary Historical Society is in Washington, DC, its purpose ostensibly for literary analysis, advance and achievement. No one goes there and takes tours -- they can't get past the main desk without proper clearance. In reality, it's a CIA office where people read and analyze mystery and spy novels (what a dream job!) to seek out correlations between fiction and fact. <br /><br />One of the employees there, Ronald Malcolm, advises another employee (Heidegger) to ignore it when he finds a record for two crates of books that the society never received, but for which they had paid. Malcolm's advice was not followed. Shortly after this, it's Malcolm's turn to go out and get lunch for the group, which he does, taking his time. Upon his return, he finds everyone at the society dead. Sizing up the situation, he realizes that now he's in danger, and he does what he's been trained to do: calls the panic line at CIA headquarters, where he identifies himself as Condor. From this point, things go horribly wrong for Malcolm, and he finds himself on the run, with his life on the line.<br /><br />An awesome book -- you seriously don't know who you can trust in this story which heightens the experience and the aura of suspense which builds throughout. Even 34 years later this book still has the ability to keep you turning pages. Recommended for people who enjoy espionage fiction, suspense or people who like stories about the CIA.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3780394882583141152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1645991608" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1645991608" />
    <a title="Karen B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5230033-karen-b"><img alt="Karen B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308784537p2/5230033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1645991608?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen B." href="/user/show/5230033-karen-b">Karen B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13148488-six-days-of-the-condor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=audible-books">audible-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645991608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8499243346834273322">I'm not one to usually read spy novels but seeing that this book was the basis for the movie (titled <i> Three Days of the Condor </i> ) I had to find out why the difference in titles. The author gives a great explanation of this and more about how the Russians ended up modeling a section of their spy network based on the movie. Luckily I had just enough memory of the movie, but not enough to interfere with the enjoyment of the book. This book is fast-paced and was a quick read. It kept me glued to the</span>
  <span id="freeText8499243346834273322" style="display:none">I'm not one to usually read spy novels but seeing that this book was the basis for the movie (titled <i> Three Days of the Condor </i> ) I had to find out why the difference in titles. The author gives a great explanation of this and more about how the Russians ended up modeling a section of their spy network based on the movie. Luckily I had just enough memory of the movie, but not enough to interfere with the enjoyment of the book. This book is fast-paced and was a quick read. It kept me glued to the book which made it great reading (and listening) for me. (The narrator of the audio book did such a great job that I later looked for other audio books that he narrated.) The plot is described in the write up about the book. I was fascinated by the concept that this fictional section of the CIA read books as their "job" and particularly Malcolm (Condor's) assignment. I also enjoyed the writer's description of the various branches of the intelligence community. Now I want to see the movie again!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8499243346834273322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_419207548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419207548" />
    <a title="Mart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8106181-mart"><img alt="Mart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407669884p2/8106181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419207548?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mart" href="/user/show/8106181-mart">Mart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419207548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6549087836965680422">"Da Vinci Code" and other similar modern conspiracy thrillers are a well developed, refined product category. They have several intertwined subplots, plenty of surprising twists and substantial character development. <br/><br/>"Six Days of the Condor" is one of the foundation lying books of this genre. It's an early model. It's like a 70ties car compared to new, 2012 vehicles. It has everything, but everything is just far shittier in every regard. The plot is very simple. There are no twists (that's an ex</span>
  <span id="freeText6549087836965680422" style="display:none">"Da Vinci Code" and other similar modern conspiracy thrillers are a well developed, refined product category. They have several intertwined subplots, plenty of surprising twists and substantial character development. <br /><br />"Six Days of the Condor" is one of the foundation lying books of this genre. It's an early model. It's like a 70ties car compared to new, 2012 vehicles. It has everything, but everything is just far shittier in every regard. The plot is very simple. There are no twists (that's an extra that appeared on later models). The characters have just about as much individuality as a dull plastic gear shift lever.<br /><br />All in all, if you're interested in historic spy thrillers, then go ahead, read it. Otherwise just get yourself a newer model.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6549087836965680422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/683065049" />

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer683065049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1103544975077467510">Clumsily written (the author even used 'lay' where he meant 'lie,' which brings to mind the eternal question: where were the editors?), badly plotted, this thriller bears little resemblance to the very fine, taut Sydney Pollack/Robert Redford film made from it ("Three Days of the Condor," which should tip you that Pollack and screenplay writer Lorenzo Semple know more than Grady about pacing). In every instance where the moviemakers veered from the plot they bettered the story. This is one of th</span>
  <span id="freeText1103544975077467510" style="display:none">Clumsily written (the author even used 'lay' where he meant 'lie,' which brings to mind the eternal question: where were the editors?), badly plotted, this thriller bears little resemblance to the very fine, taut Sydney Pollack/Robert Redford film made from it ("Three Days of the Condor," which should tip you that Pollack and screenplay writer Lorenzo Semple know more than Grady about pacing). In every instance where the moviemakers veered from the plot they bettered the story. This is one of those rare cases where the movie is much better than the book. A few others come to mind: "Jaws," "The Godfather," "The Shining," "Gone with the Wind," "Big Trouble," and maybe "Election." </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12595398562007845425">I picked up this book while scanning the mystery shelves at my local library. I had seen the movie and enjoyed it, but then Robert Redford was 40 years younger and easy on the eye. The book has the same plot line, but the endings are significantly different. The book is dated, but I actually enjoyed that the story proceeded without cell phones and home computers. It was a pleasure to see how the protagonist must use his skills to survive. I enjoyed the short rapid fire sentences, and the concurr</span>
  <span id="freeText12595398562007845425" style="display:none">I picked up this book while scanning the mystery shelves at my local library. I had seen the movie and enjoyed it, but then Robert Redford was 40 years younger and easy on the eye. The book has the same plot line, but the endings are significantly different. The book is dated, but I actually enjoyed that the story proceeded without cell phones and home computers. It was a pleasure to see how the protagonist must use his skills to survive. I enjoyed the short rapid fire sentences, and the concurrent action with the various characters in the book. The book is a quick read and I would most definitely recommend it to anyone who likes a well constructed mystery.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2635599449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14311792240340706846">Terrifically taut thriller that is totally of its time, with obligatory 70s sex scenes, baddies performing karate chops and old men in old money houses still in charge. The story races along, driven by a ridiculous number of lucky coincidences, both good and bad. Along the way, Condor does actually use his brains to keep ahead of the people coming after him and it's that sense of the plucky amateur which fed into the Redford movie and has become a trope of all "accidental fugitive" stories. In a</span>
  <span id="freeText14311792240340706846" style="display:none">Terrifically taut thriller that is totally of its time, with obligatory 70s sex scenes, baddies performing karate chops and old men in old money houses still in charge. The story races along, driven by a ridiculous number of lucky coincidences, both good and bad. Along the way, Condor does actually use his brains to keep ahead of the people coming after him and it's that sense of the plucky amateur which fed into the Redford movie and has become a trope of all "accidental fugitive" stories. In and out in under 150 pages, there was very little here not to love.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14311792240340706846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426471816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13321664104556417796"><strong>An entertaining but stereotypical novel </strong><br/><br/>I enjoyed this book as an entertaining spy thriller, that was a light enough, escapist read. I knew this story as an old Robert Redford movie. And actually I was reminded of Robert Ludlum’s Jason Bourne novels (which are much better in every way actually). My single complaint was the writer used a few too many coincidental moments to opportunely move the story forward. The worst was in the end when a bad guy confessed everything out of the blue to the hero</span>
  <span id="freeText13321664104556417796" style="display:none"><strong>An entertaining but stereotypical novel </strong><br /><br />I enjoyed this book as an entertaining spy thriller, that was a light enough, escapist read. I knew this story as an old Robert Redford movie. And actually I was reminded of Robert Ludlum’s Jason Bourne novels (which are much better in every way actually). My single complaint was the writer used a few too many coincidental moments to opportunely move the story forward. The worst was in the end when a bad guy confessed everything out of the blue to the hero, tying up all the lose ends. How convenient to use this stereotypical writer’s cop out. I enjoy this genre of story and might read more in the series in the future just to see if the author grew in writing skill as the series progressed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13321664104556417796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13391704039765344620">Newly issued A Mysterious Press, this 2016 edition has a 20-page introduction by James Grady as a bonus, giving background about the development, writing, research, movie-making, and repercussions of Six Days of the Condor. Mr. Grady writes much like a screen-writer and has a journalistic prose. He plain style makes the espionage even more suspenseful and believable for me. Surveillance, avoidance, interactions aren't hyped but rather mundane and/or show thought behind them. This, and a fiction </span>
  <span id="freeText13391704039765344620" style="display:none">Newly issued A Mysterious Press, this 2016 edition has a 20-page introduction by James Grady as a bonus, giving background about the development, writing, research, movie-making, and repercussions of Six Days of the Condor. Mr. Grady writes much like a screen-writer and has a journalistic prose. He plain style makes the espionage even more suspenseful and believable for me. Surveillance, avoidance, interactions aren't hyped but rather mundane and/or show thought behind them. This, and a fiction dealing with CIA were unique for the time, particularly in that era of James Bond flash-bang entertainments. Lastly, I liked James Grady's style of transition from one scene to another one happening at the same time...this method also seen in the Argentine political mystery Betty Boo by Claudia Pineiro.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935116708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11762867167898469410">Read the book because I greatly enjoyed the Robert Redford-Faye Dunaway movie which was based on the book. But the book is nothing like the movie; the plot is completely different, the characters have different names, and the ending is a surprise. The movie was about a CIA analyst who escapes a mass assassination at his office and must figure out what is going on as he eludes further attempts on his life with the help of a beautiful woman. The book was about ex-CIA killers from the Vietnam War d</span>
  <span id="freeText11762867167898469410" style="display:none">Read the book because I greatly enjoyed the Robert Redford-Faye Dunaway movie which was based on the book. But the book is nothing like the movie; the plot is completely different, the characters have different names, and the ending is a surprise. The movie was about a CIA analyst who escapes a mass assassination at his office and must figure out what is going on as he eludes further attempts on his life with the help of a beautiful woman. The book was about ex-CIA killers from the Vietnam War days who are now involved in drug running; the plot is similar to the movie, Lethal Weapon 2. The book ends in a violent fight between the hero and a hitman in an airport bathroom. I credit the author with describing the fight in words that made the action come alive better than a movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11762867167898469410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2174617848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2174617848" />
    <a title="Alberto" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61486263-alberto"><img alt="Alberto" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479848220p2/61486263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174617848?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alberto" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alberto" href="/user/show/61486263-alberto">Alberto</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61486263-alberto?shelf=spy">spy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61486263-alberto?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61486263-alberto?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61486263-alberto?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174617848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10981730863245260389">The book is written in a style that I liked a lot. Simple, no euphemisms, and flowing. Simply a good thriller. Like the majority of people, I watched the film first when I was younger (but it's called instead "Three days of the Condor") and then realized that it was based on this novel. The book is a very good thriller, captivating from the beginning.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35645863-lena?shelf=audio">audio</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369891843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7590550838664106039"><strong>Spies. Intrigue. Action. Sex. Murder.</strong><br/>These are a few of my favorite things! At last a classic that exceeds expectations! It was fast paced, relevant, intelligent, and short. A must read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iYVEK5J4DhYQBi019QsYW3fO1h7h1SKqU9x3wKjM+tIvIGsHFbs4A6lrzdpSlK5GUGPswiVnOkqnuzlD5qN+oQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wkq0AoO0dIEspkgJQESd1SA0CzCXWFP4SVL4yaQxACj875suBHdClJXLqObn2yvIB5kx7FPqSxi9NbZK6l6EWw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6501001551910046742">James Grady is a longtime author of thrillers, police procedural and espionage novels. He graduated from the University of Montana School of Journalism in 1974. During college, he worked for United States Senator Lee Metcalf of Montana as an staff member.<br/><br/>From 1974 - 1978 he was an investigative journalist for the famous muckraker Jack Anderson. Best known as the author of <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2579284.Six_Days_of_the_Condor' title='Six Days of the Condor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Six Days of the Condor</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText6501001551910046742" style="display:none">James Grady is a longtime author of thrillers, police procedural and espionage novels. He graduated from the University of Montana School of Journalism in 1974. During college, he worked for United States Senator Lee Metcalf of Montana as an staff member.<br /><br />From 1974 - 1978 he was an investigative journalist for the famous muckraker Jack Anderson. Best known as the author of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2579284.Six_Days_of_the_Condor" title="Six Days of the Condor" rel="nofollow noopener">Six Days of the Condor</a>
</i>, which was adapted to film as <i>Three Days of the Condor</i> starring <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16915.Robert_Redford" title="Robert Redford" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Redford</a> in 1975.<br /><br />James Grady has gone on to write almost a dozen more novels in the thirty-eight years since <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2579284.Six_Days_of_the_Condor" title="Six Days of the Condor" rel="nofollow noopener">Six Days of the Condor</a>
</i> was published. <br /><br />In the past James Grady has written under the pseudonyms of James Dalton and Brit Shelby.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6501001551910046742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
